Text: Abstract, Font: CMBX10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: We discuss the seminal article in which Le Bellac and L´evy-Leblond have, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: identiﬁed two Galilean limits of electromagnetism [1], and its modern implica-, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: tions. We use their results to point out some confusion in the literature and, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: in the teaching of special relativity and electromagnetism. For instance, it is, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: not widely recognized that there exist, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text:  two, Font: CMTI10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text:  well deﬁned non-relativistic limits,, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: so that researchers and teachers are likely to utilize an incoherent mixture of, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: both. Recent works have shed a new light on the choice of gauge conditions, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: in classical electromagnetism. We retrieve Le Bellac-L´evy-Leblond’s results by, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: examining orders of magnitudes, and then with a Lorentz-like manifestly co-, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: variant approach to Galilean covariance based on a 5-dimensional Minkowski, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: manifold. We emphasize the Riemann-Lorenz approach based on the vector and, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: scalar potentials as opposed to the Heaviside-Hertz formulation in terms of elec-, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: tromagnetic ﬁelds. We discuss various applications and experiments, such as, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: in magnetohydrodynamics and electrohydrodynamics, quantum mechanics, su-, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: perconductivity, continuous media, etc. Much of the current technology where, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: waves are not taken into account, is actually based on Galilean electromag-, Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: netism., Font: CMR10, Size: 10.909099578857422
Text: Key words: Galilean covariance, special relativity, electromagnetism, four-potential., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125

Text: Introduction, Font: CMBX12, Size: 17.21540069580078
Text: The purpose of this article is to emphasize the relevance of Galilean covariance in, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: physics, even nowadays, about one hundred years after Lorentz, Poincar´e and Ein-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: stein, then facing the apparent incompatibility between Galilean mechanics and the, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: full set of Maxwell equations, have developed a theory that turned into special rel-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: ativity [2]. Seventy years later, Le Bellac and L´evy-Leblond (LBLL) observed that, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: there exist not only one, but, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text:  two, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text:  well-deﬁned Galilean (that is, non-relativistic) limits, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: of electromagnetism: the so-called ‘magnetic’ and ‘electric’ limits [1]. Although spe-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: cial relativity has superseded Galilean relativity when it comes to the description of, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: high energy phenomena, there exists a wealth of low-energy systems, particularly in, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: condensed matter physics and low-energy nuclear physics, where Galilean covariance, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: should not be ignored., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: We wish to point out hereafter some confusion which results from not recognizing, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: appropriately the two Galilean limits of electromagnetism. This follows from inacu-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: rate deﬁnitions of non-relativistic covariance, which is why we emphasize at once that, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: the deﬁnition of Galilean covariance employed henceforth in this paper rests on its, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: compatibility with the Galilean transformations of space-time (Eq. (6), below). Ex-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: amples of misleading, though well known, such text presentations are mentioned in, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125

Text: Therefore, let us point out forcefully that the choice of a gauge condition is dictated, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: by the relativistic versus Galilean nature of the problem. The Lorenz gauge condition, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: must be chosen in the relativistic context as well as in the electric Galilean limit. The, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Coulomb gauge condition can be chosen only in the magnetic limit. For example, this, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: implies that quantization in the Coulomb gauge of light waves is prohibited because, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: of Galilean covariance and must be re-examined., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: We refer to a discussion of the, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: physical meaning that one can ascribe to the various gauge conditions [14]., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: From the historical point of view, Galilean electromagnetism has shed a new light, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: on the pre-relativity era. Indeed, a careful reading of James Clerk Maxwell’s famous, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Treatise on Electricity and Magnetism, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text:  reveals that he has employed the electric limit, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: when dealing with dielectrics in his ﬁrst volume [20]. On the other hand, in his sec-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: ond volume, he used the magnetic limit when dealing with ohmic conductors, except, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: 13, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: toward the end, where he introduced into the magnetic limit equations the so-called, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: displacement current ‘by hand’ in order to demonstrate that light is a transverse, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: electromagnetic wave [20]. But, as we have seen in the particular case of the electric, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: limit (and it is also valid in relativity), the displacement current follows from choos-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: ing the Lorenz gauge whereas Maxwell (wrongfully!) kept the Coulomb gauge within, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: the relativistic context for the ﬁelds. This diﬃculty enticed Hertz and Heaviside to, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: abandon potentials and to cast Maxwell’s equations in terms of ﬁelds rather than po-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: tentials. Albert Einstein read Hertz’ papers on the topic and subsequently employed, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Maxwell equations in terms of the ﬁelds (the Heaviside-Hertz formulation) whereas, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125

Text: 4.7, Font: CMBX12, Size: 14.346199989318848
Text: Electrodynamics of moving bodies at low velocities, Font: CMBX12, Size: 14.346199989318848
Text: Galilean electromagnetism raises severe doubts concerning our current understanding, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: of the electrodynamics of moving media. Indeed, several experiments, like the ones, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: by Roentgen [34], Eichenwald [35], Wilson [36], Wilson and Wilson [37], Trouton and, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Noble [38], etc., were believed to corroborate special relativity. As we will demonstrate, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: for the Trouton-Noble experiment, there is not always a need for special relativity, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: because the typical relative velocity in these experiments is well below the speed of, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: light. Then, the question is whether the above mentioned experiments be explained, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: by either the electric limit, the magnetic limit or a combination of both., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: 4.7.1, Font: CMBX12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: The Trouton-Noble experiment, Font: CMBX12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: The Trouton-Noble’s experiment is thought to be the electromagnetic analogue of, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: the optical Michelson and Morley experiment [38]. It was designed in order to show, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: whether one can observe a mechanical velocity of the ether if one considers that the, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: luminiferous medium should be a medium whose parts can be followed mechanically., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Like the null result of Michelson-Morley’s optical experiment, the Trouton-Noble, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: experiment was negative in the sense that one was not able to detect either an absolute, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: motion with respect to the ether, or a partial entrainment, as believed by other various, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: theories., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: 20, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: In 1905, Albert Einstein suggested to consider the ether as superﬂuous since the ex-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: periments were not able to detect a mechanical motion of it. Others, like H. Poincar´e, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: and H.A. Lorentz, were reluctant to abandon the notion of ether as the bearer of the, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: electromagnetic ﬁeld, despite the fact that they have adopted the relativity princi-, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: ple. However, in 1920, Einstein recoursed to the ether as the bearer of the metric, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: allowing the propagation of gravitational waves, at a conference in Leyden. Today,, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: even though the ether is a banished word in modern science, one can use it as did the, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: older Einstein in order to describe the vacuum with physical (though not mechanical), Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: properties., Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125

Text: 4.7.2, Font: CMBX12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: “Einstein asymmetry”, Font: CMBX12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: In his famous article on the electrodynamics of moving media, Albert Einstein pointed, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: out the importance of whether or not one should ascribe energy to the ﬁelds when, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: dealing with motion [40]. We reproduced here the introduction of his paper:, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: “It is known that Maxwell’s electrodynamics -as usually understood at the present, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: time- when applied to moving bodies, leads to asymmetries which do not appear to be, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: inherent in the phenomena. Take, for example, the reciprocal electrodynamic action, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: 22, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: of a magnet and a conductor. The observable phenomenon here depends only on the, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: relative motion of the conductor and the magnet, whereas the customary view draws, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: a sharp distinction between the two cases in which either one or the other of these, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: bodies is in motion. For if the magnet is in motion and the conductor at rest, there, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: arises in the neighbourhood of the magnet an electric ﬁeld with a certain deﬁnite en-, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: ergy, producing a current at the places where parts of the conductor are situated. But, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: if the magnet is stationary and the conductor in motion, then no electric ﬁeld arises, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: in the neighbourhood of the magnet. In the conductor, however, we ﬁnd an electro-, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: motive force to which in itself there is no corresponding energy, but which gives rise, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: -assuming equality of relative motion in the two cases discussed- to electric currents, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: of the same path and intensity as those produced by the electric forces in the former, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: case.”, Font: CMTI12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: Like our discussion of the Trouton-Noble experiment, the magnetic Poynting’s, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: theorem can explain why one cannot ascribe an energy to the motional electric ﬁeld, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
Text: in Einstein’s thought experiment:, Font: CMR12, Size: 11.9552001953125
